{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-sonnet-4-6","id":"msg_01HyvD7bar5wJLahJnhb2Dbm","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01F4yihnVaJtkEeuwEnsqvH3","name":"Write","input":{"path":"/workspace/security_audit.md","content":"# Security Audit: Ceph RADOS Gateway S3 Authentication\n\n**Date:** 2026-03-08  \n**Scope:** AWS Signature V2/V4 authentication implementation in `src/rgw/`  \n**Repository:** `github.com/sg-evals/ceph--v19.2.1`\n\n---\n\n## 1. Authentication Flow Overview\n\nThe S3 authentication flow in Ceph RGW is implemented across the following files:\n\n| File | Role |\n|------|------|\n| `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.h` | Auth strategy classes, V4 constants, time-skew check declaration |\n| `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc` | Canonical header/query construction, signing-key derivation, V2/V4 HMAC computation |\n| `src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.h` | `AWSEngine`, `VersionAbstractor`, V2/V4 abstractor class declarations |\n| `src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc` | Auth data extraction, version detection, `LocalEngine::authenticate()` |\n| `src/rgw/rgw_auth.h` | Core `Identity` and `Engine` interfaces |\n\n### Key Functions\n\n```\nAWSGeneralAbstractor::get_auth_data()     rgw_rest_s3.cc:5556\n  └─ discover_aws_flavour()               → determines V2 or V4\n  └─ get_auth_data_v2()                   rgw_rest_s3.cc:5988  (HMAC-SHA1)\n  └─ get_auth_data_v4()                   rgw_rest_s3.cc:5570  (HMAC-SHA256)\n\nLocalEngine::authenticate()               rgw_rest_s3.cc:6265\n  └─ signature_factory(cct, k.key, ...)   → compute server-side signature\n  └─ signature.compare(server_signature)  → compare (line 6319)\n\nget_v4_signature()                        rgw_auth_s3.cc:1013\n  └─ get_v4_signing_key()                 → HMAC-SHA256 key derivation chain\n  └─ calc_hmac_sha256(signing_key, ...)   → final digest\n\nget_v2_signature()                        rgw_auth_s3.cc:1037\n  └─ calc_hmac_sha1(secret_key, ...)      → HMAC-SHA1 digest + base64\n\nis_time_skew_ok()                         rgw_auth_s3.cc:265\n  └─ RGW_AUTH_GRACE = 15 minutes          rgw_auth_s3.h:30\n```\n\n---\n\n## 2. Security Findings\n\n---\n\n### Finding 1 — Non-Constant-Time Signature Comparison (Timing Attack)\n\n**Severity:** High  \n**File:** `src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc`, line 6319  \n**File:** `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc`, lines 1228, 1231\n\n#### Description\n\nThe final signature comparison in `LocalEngine::authenticate()` uses `std::string::compare()`, which is **not constant-time**. An attacker can exploit measurable timing differences to learn, one byte at a time, whether a forged signature prefix matches the expected server signature. This enables a remote timing oracle attack against HMAC-SHA256 (V4) and HMAC-SHA1 (V2) signatures.\n\n#### Code Reference\n\n```cpp\n// src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc:6317-6330\nconst VersionAbstractor::server_signature_t server_signature = \\\n  signature_factory(cct, k.key, string_to_sign);\nauto compare = signature.compare(server_signature);   // <-- NOT constant-time\n\nldpp_dout(dpp, 15) << \"server signature=\" << server_signature << dendl;\nldpp_dout(dpp, 15) << \"client signature=\" << signature << dendl;\n\nif (compare != 0) {\n  return result_t::reject(-ERR_SIGNATURE_NO_MATCH);\n}\n```\n\nThe same issue appears in chunk signature verification:\n\n```cpp\n// src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc:1225-1232\nauto match_signatures = [&]() -> bool {\n  if (chunk_meta.get_offset() == 0) [[unlikely]] {\n    return chunk_meta.get_signature() == prev_chunk_signature;  // <-- NOT constant-time\n  }\n  return chunk_meta.get_signature() == calc_signature;          // <-- NOT constant-time\n};\n```\n\n`std::string::operator==` and `std::string::compare()` are permitted by the C++ standard to short-circuit on the first mismatched byte, exposing timing differences measurable over a network in controlled conditions.\n\n#### Remediation\n\nReplace all signature comparisons with a constant-time comparison function such as `CRYPTO_memcmp()` (OpenSSL), `timingsafe_bcmp()` (BSD), or a dedicated implementation:\n\n```cpp\n// Constant-time comparison\nbool signatures_equal = (server_signature.size() == signature.size()) &&\n    (CRYPTO_memcmp(server_signature.data(),\n                   signature.data(),\n                   server_signature.size()) == 0);\nif (!signatures_equal) {\n  return result_t::reject(-ERR_SIGNATURE_NO_MATCH);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### Finding 2 — AWS Signature Version 2 (HMAC-SHA1) Supported Without Restriction\n\n**Severity:** High  \n**File:** `src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc`, lines 5556–5574, 5988–6068  \n**File:** `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc`, lines 1037–1062\n\n#### Description\n\nThe gateway transparently supports AWS Signature Version 2, which uses **HMAC-SHA1** with a significantly weaker security posture than V4:\n\n- SHA-1 is considered **cryptographically broken** for collision resistance (though HMAC-SHA1 is still preimage-resistant, it offers only 80-bit security).\n- V2 does **not** include the HTTP body or most headers in the signed material, making it vulnerable to request body substitution attacks.\n- V2 presigned URLs use an epoch-based `Expires` value and are not protected against relay attacks across regions.\n- AWS itself deprecated Signature V2 and began blocking it in regions after 2020.\n\nThe version selection is fully transparent to the server — whichever version the client presents is accepted, with no operator-visible warning:\n\n```cpp\n// src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc:5555-5574\nAWSGeneralAbstractor::get_auth_data(const req_state* const s) const\n{\n  AwsVersion version;\n  AwsRoute route;\n  std::tie(version, route) = discover_aws_flavour(s->info);\n  // ...\n  if (version == AwsVersion::V2) {\n    return get_auth_data_v2(s);           // uses HMAC-SHA1\n  } else if (version == AwsVersion::V4) {\n    return get_auth_data_v4(s, ...);      // uses HMAC-SHA256\n  }\n}\n\n// src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc:1037-1062\nget_v2_signature(CephContext* const cct,\n                 const std::string& secret_key,\n                 const AWSEngine::VersionAbstractor::string_to_sign_t& string_to_sign)\n{\n  // ...\n  const auto digest = calc_hmac_sha1(secret_key, string_to_sign);  // HMAC-SHA1\n  // ...\n}\n```\n\n#### Remediation\n\n1. Add a Ceph configuration option (e.g., `rgw_s3_auth_require_sigv4`) to **deny V2 requests** in production deployments.\n2. Log a warning at operator-visible log level (0 or 1) whenever a V2 request is accepted.\n3. Audit presigned-URL handling separately — V2 presigned URLs allow body substitution because `Content-MD5` inclusion is optional in V2's canonical string.\n\n```ini\n# Recommended ceph.conf setting\n[client.rgw]\nrgw s3 auth require sigv4 = true\n```\n\n---\n\n### Finding 3 — 15-Minute Replay Attack Window\n\n**Severity:** Medium  \n**File:** `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.h`, line 30  \n**File:** `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc`, lines 265–278, 457–458\n\n#### Description\n\nThe request timestamp validation window (`RGW_AUTH_GRACE`) is set to **15 minutes** in both directions:\n\n```cpp\n// src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.h:30\nstatic constexpr auto RGW_AUTH_GRACE = std::chrono::minutes{15};\n\n// src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc:265-278\nbool is_time_skew_ok(time_t t)\n{\n  auto req_tp = ceph::coarse_real_clock::from_time_t(t);\n  auto cur_tp = ceph::coarse_real_clock::now();\n\n  if (std::chrono::abs(cur_tp - req_tp) > RGW_AUTH_GRACE) {\n    dout(10) << \"NOTICE: request time skew too big.\" << dendl;\n    return false;\n  }\n  return true;\n}\n```\n\nThis is applied on V4 header-auth requests at `rgw_rest_s3.cc:457`. However, it is **not applied** to V2 presigned URLs (which use a fixed `Expires` epoch time instead) or V4 presigned URLs (which carry their own `X-Amz-Expires` duration, validated separately in `parse_v4_query_string` at `rgw_auth_s3.cc:308-318`).\n\nA 15-minute window means any captured signed request (e.g., intercepted over HTTP without TLS, or obtained from logs) can be replayed for up to 15 minutes. Since there is **no nonce or request ID tracking**, identical requests from different clients are indistinguishable and will both succeed within the window.\n\nThe V4 presigned URL expiry is validated:\n```cpp\n// src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc:314-319\nuint64_t req_sec = (uint64_t)internal_timegm(&date_t);\nuint64_t now = ceph_clock_now();\nif (now >= req_sec + exp) {\n  return -ERR_PRESIGNED_URL_EXPIRED;\n}\n```\nBut again, replay within the window is not prevented.\n\n#### Remediation\n\n1. Make `RGW_AUTH_GRACE` configurable via a Ceph config option (e.g., `rgw_auth_grace_seconds`), allowing operators to reduce it to 5 minutes or less for high-security deployments.\n2. Consider implementing a short-lived nonce/replay cache (e.g., LRU-bounded set of recently seen request signatures with TTL equal to the grace window). This prevents replays within the window at the cost of additional memory and coordination overhead.\n3. Ensure that deployments use TLS to reduce interception risk.\n\n---\n\n### Finding 4 — Unsigned Payload Accepted by Default\n\n**Severity:** Medium  \n**File:** `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.h`, lines 637–659  \n**File:** `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc`, lines 672–675\n\n#### Description\n\nWhen the `x-amz-content-sha256` header is absent from a request, the implementation silently defaults to `UNSIGNED-PAYLOAD`, meaning the HTTP request body is **not included in the signed material** and is not integrity-verified:\n\n```cpp\n// src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.h:637-659\nstatic inline const char* get_v4_exp_payload_hash(const req_info& info)\n{\n  const char *expected_request_payload_hash = \\\n    info.env->get(\"HTTP_X_AMZ_CONTENT_SHA256\");\n\n  if (!expected_request_payload_hash) {\n    /* ... */\n    expected_request_payload_hash = AWS4_UNSIGNED_PAYLOAD_HASH;  // \"UNSIGNED-PAYLOAD\"\n  }\n  return expected_request_payload_hash;\n}\n\n// src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.h:672-675\nstatic inline bool is_v4_payload_unsigned(const char* const exp_payload_hash)\n{\n  return boost::contains(exp_payload_hash, \"UNSIGNED-PAYLOAD\");\n}\n```\n\nWhen `is_v4_payload_unsigned()` returns true, the payload completers (`AWSv4ComplSingle`, `AWSv4ComplMulti`) skip body-hash verification. This means an on-path attacker who intercepts a signed request can **modify the request body** without invalidating the signature.\n\nThe `FLAG_UNSIGNED_CHUNKED` flag similarly short-circuits all chunk signature verification:\n\n```cpp\n// src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc:1207-1209\nif (flags & FLAG_UNSIGNED_CHUNKED) {\n  return false;   // no verification at all\n}\n```\n\n#### Remediation\n\n1. Add a server-side configuration option to **reject requests with `UNSIGNED-PAYLOAD`** for write operations (PUT, POST, DELETE) on sensitive buckets or globally.\n2. Log a warning when unsigned payload is accepted for write operations.\n3. Require clients to send `x-amz-content-sha256` with an actual hash for all mutating requests in high-security environments.\n\n---\n\n### Finding 5 — Sensitive Data in Debug Logs\n\n**Severity:** Low  \n**File:** `src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc`, lines 6321–6326  \n**File:** `src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc`, lines 6053–6054\n\n#### Description\n\nBoth the client-supplied signature and the server-computed signature are emitted to the Ceph debug log at verbosity level 15. The `string_to_sign` (which encodes the canonical request and timestamp) is logged at level 10:\n\n```cpp\n// src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc:6321-6326\nldpp_dout(dpp, 15) << \"string_to_sign=\"\n               << rgw::crypt_sanitize::log_content{string_to_sign}\n               << dendl;\nldpp_dout(dpp, 15) << \"server signature=\" << server_signature << dendl;\nldpp_dout(dpp, 15) << \"client signature=\" << signature << dendl;\nldpp_dout(dpp, 15) << \"compare=\" << compare << dendl;\n```\n\nWhile verbosity 15 is rarely enabled in production, if an operator temporarily enables debug logging to diagnose an issue, these entries will appear in plaintext in log files. The `rgw::crypt_sanitize::log_content` wrapper in V4 contexts only provides protection when the sanitize guard is active; for V2, `string_to_sign` is logged without consistent sanitization:\n\n```cpp\n// src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc:6053-6054\nldpp_dout(s, 10) << \"string_to_sign:\\n\"\n               << rgw::crypt_sanitize::auth{s,string_to_sign} << dendl;\n```\n\nThe signing key intermediate values are also logged in `get_v4_signing_key()` at level 10:\n\n```cpp\n// src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc:996-999\nldpp_dout(dpp, 10) << \"date_k    = \" << date_k << dendl;\nldpp_dout(dpp, 10) << \"region_k  = \" << region_k << dendl;\nldpp_dout(dpp, 10) << \"service_k = \" << service_k << dendl;\nldpp_dout(dpp, 10) << \"signing_k = \" << signing_key << dendl;\n```\n\nIntermediate HMAC keys `date_k`, `region_k`, `service_k`, and `signing_key` are derived from the secret key and fully expose it — an attacker with access to the logs can reconstruct requests and forge signatures.\n\n#### Remediation\n\n1. Move all signature value and signing-key-chain log entries to verbosity level 20 or higher.\n2. Replace plaintext emission of `signing_key` (and intermediate keys) with redacted placeholders or remove these log lines entirely.\n3. Ensure that any log file containing RGW debug output has restrictive filesystem permissions (mode 0600) owned by the RGW process user.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Summary Risk Assessment\n\n| # | Finding | Severity | Exploitability | Impact |\n|---|---------|----------|----------------|--------|\n| 1 | Non-constant-time signature comparison (timing oracle) | **High** | Moderate (requires many requests, network precision) | Full auth bypass possible over time |\n| 2 | AWS Signature V2 (HMAC-SHA1) accepted without restriction | **High** | Low–Moderate (requires downgrade or legacy client) | Weaker algorithm; body substitution possible |\n| 3 | 15-minute replay attack window, no nonce tracking | **Medium** | Low (requires request interception) | Captured signed requests replayable |\n| 4 | Unsigned payload accepted by default | **Medium** | Moderate (requires MITM position) | Body integrity not guaranteed on write ops |\n| 5 | Signing-key chain and signatures emitted to debug logs | **Low** | Low (requires log access) | Key material / signature exposure |\n\n### Overall Risk Rating: **High**\n\nThe combination of a timing-oracle in signature comparison (Finding 1) and continued support for the deprecated SHA-1-based V2 protocol (Finding 2) represents the most significant risk. Both are independently exploitable and together significantly weaken the authentication guarantees that S3 signature verification is intended to provide.\n\n### Recommended Immediate Actions\n\n1. **Replace `signature.compare()` with a constant-time comparison** (Finding 1) — low-effort, high-impact fix.\n2. **Add `rgw_s3_auth_require_sigv4` configuration option** and enable it by default or in security-hardened deployments (Finding 2).\n3. **Make `RGW_AUTH_GRACE` configurable** and reduce it to 5 minutes in new deployments (Finding 3).\n4. **Remove or raise verbosity of signing-key log entries** in `get_v4_signing_key()` (Finding 5).\n\n---\n\n*Audit performed by static analysis of source code. No dynamic testing was conducted. Findings reflect code-level vulnerabilities; actual exploitability may vary depending on network topology, TLS deployment, and operator configuration.*\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":3634,"cache_read_input_tokens":51032,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":3634,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":8,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"c88aed4d-2e4d-45dd-9dd5-999fcfab4d26","uuid":"61117f62-8e3b-4d32-b202-e95bf7c8fc14"}

{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-sonnet-4-6","id":"msg_01NbCYwTkDWzKUiLvcgZdp18","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01BTHQEdbPrNenANN1m3oefP","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/security_audit.md","content":"# Security Audit: Ceph RADOS Gateway S3 Authentication\n\n**Date:** 2026-03-08\n**Scope:** AWS Signature V2/V4 authentication implementation in `src/rgw/`\n**Repository:** `github.com/sg-evals/ceph--v19.2.1`\n\n---\n\n## 1. Authentication Flow Overview\n\nThe S3 authentication flow in Ceph RGW is implemented across the following files:\n\n| File | Role |\n|------|------|\n| `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.h` | Auth strategy classes, V4 constants, time-skew check declaration |\n| `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc` | Canonical header/query construction, signing-key derivation, V2/V4 HMAC computation |\n| `src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.h` | `AWSEngine`, `VersionAbstractor`, V2/V4 abstractor class declarations |\n| `src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc` | Auth data extraction, version detection, `LocalEngine::authenticate()` |\n| `src/rgw/rgw_auth.h` | Core `Identity` and `Engine` interfaces |\n\n### Key Functions\n\n```\nAWSGeneralAbstractor::get_auth_data()     rgw_rest_s3.cc:5556\n  └─ discover_aws_flavour()               → determines V2 or V4\n  └─ get_auth_data_v2()                   rgw_rest_s3.cc:5988  (HMAC-SHA1)\n  └─ get_auth_data_v4()                   rgw_rest_s3.cc:5570  (HMAC-SHA256)\n\nLocalEngine::authenticate()               rgw_rest_s3.cc:6265\n  └─ signature_factory(cct, k.key, ...)   → compute server-side signature\n  └─ signature.compare(server_signature)  → compare (line 6319)\n\nget_v4_signature()                        rgw_auth_s3.cc:1013\n  └─ get_v4_signing_key()                 → HMAC-SHA256 key derivation chain\n  └─ calc_hmac_sha256(signing_key, ...)   → final digest\n\nget_v2_signature()                        rgw_auth_s3.cc:1037\n  └─ calc_hmac_sha1(secret_key, ...)      → HMAC-SHA1 digest + base64\n\nis_time_skew_ok()                         rgw_auth_s3.cc:265\n  └─ RGW_AUTH_GRACE = 15 minutes          rgw_auth_s3.h:30\n```\n\n---\n\n## 2. Security Findings\n\n---\n\n### Finding 1 — Non-Constant-Time Signature Comparison (Timing Attack)\n\n**Severity:** High\n**File:** `src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc`, line 6319\n**File:** `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc`, lines 1228, 1231\n\n#### Description\n\nThe final signature comparison in `LocalEngine::authenticate()` uses `std::string::compare()`, which is **not constant-time**. An attacker can exploit measurable timing differences to learn, one byte at a time, whether a forged signature prefix matches the expected server signature. This enables a remote timing oracle attack against HMAC-SHA256 (V4) and HMAC-SHA1 (V2) signatures.\n\n#### Code Reference\n\n```cpp\n// src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc:6317-6330\nconst VersionAbstractor::server_signature_t server_signature = \\\n  signature_factory(cct, k.key, string_to_sign);\nauto compare = signature.compare(server_signature);   // <-- NOT constant-time\n\nldpp_dout(dpp, 15) << \"server signature=\" << server_signature << dendl;\nldpp_dout(dpp, 15) << \"client signature=\" << signature << dendl;\n\nif (compare != 0) {\n  return result_t::reject(-ERR_SIGNATURE_NO_MATCH);\n}\n```\n\nThe same issue appears in chunk signature verification:\n\n```cpp\n// src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc:1225-1232\nauto match_signatures = [&]() -> bool {\n  if (chunk_meta.get_offset() == 0) [[unlikely]] {\n    return chunk_meta.get_signature() == prev_chunk_signature;  // <-- NOT constant-time\n  }\n  return chunk_meta.get_signature() == calc_signature;          // <-- NOT constant-time\n};\n```\n\n`std::string::operator==` and `std::string::compare()` are permitted by the C++ standard to short-circuit on the first mismatched byte, exposing timing differences measurable over a network in controlled conditions.\n\n#### Remediation\n\nReplace all signature comparisons with a constant-time comparison function such as `CRYPTO_memcmp()` (OpenSSL), `timingsafe_bcmp()` (BSD), or a dedicated implementation:\n\n```cpp\n// Constant-time comparison\nbool signatures_equal = (server_signature.size() == signature.size()) &&\n    (CRYPTO_memcmp(server_signature.data(),\n                   signature.data(),\n                   server_signature.size()) == 0);\nif (!signatures_equal) {\n  return result_t::reject(-ERR_SIGNATURE_NO_MATCH);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### Finding 2 — AWS Signature Version 2 (HMAC-SHA1) Supported Without Restriction\n\n**Severity:** High\n**File:** `src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc`, lines 5556–5574, 5988–6068\n**File:** `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc`, lines 1037–1062\n\n#### Description\n\nThe gateway transparently supports AWS Signature Version 2, which uses **HMAC-SHA1** with a significantly weaker security posture than V4:\n\n- SHA-1 is considered **cryptographically weakened** for collision resistance (HMAC-SHA1 offers only 80-bit security vs. 128-bit for HMAC-SHA256).\n- V2 does **not** include the HTTP body or most headers in the signed material, making it vulnerable to request body substitution attacks.\n- V2 presigned URLs use an epoch-based `Expires` value and are not protected against relay attacks across regions.\n- AWS itself deprecated Signature V2 and began blocking it in regions after 2020.\n\nThe version selection is fully transparent to the server — whichever version the client presents is accepted, with no operator-visible warning:\n\n```cpp\n// src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc:5555-5574\nAWSGeneralAbstractor::get_auth_data(const req_state* const s) const\n{\n  AwsVersion version;\n  AwsRoute route;\n  std::tie(version, route) = discover_aws_flavour(s->info);\n  // ...\n  if (version == AwsVersion::V2) {\n    return get_auth_data_v2(s);           // uses HMAC-SHA1, no warning logged\n  } else if (version == AwsVersion::V4) {\n    return get_auth_data_v4(s, ...);      // uses HMAC-SHA256\n  }\n}\n\n// src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc:1037-1062\nget_v2_signature(CephContext* const cct,\n                 const std::string& secret_key,\n                 const AWSEngine::VersionAbstractor::string_to_sign_t& string_to_sign)\n{\n  // ...\n  const auto digest = calc_hmac_sha1(secret_key, string_to_sign);  // HMAC-SHA1\n  // ...\n}\n```\n\n#### Remediation\n\n1. Add a Ceph configuration option (e.g., `rgw_s3_auth_require_sigv4`) to **deny V2 requests** in production deployments.\n2. Log a warning at operator-visible log level (0 or 1) whenever a V2 request is accepted.\n3. Audit presigned-URL handling separately — V2 presigned URLs allow body substitution because `Content-MD5` inclusion is optional in V2's canonical string.\n\n```ini\n# Recommended ceph.conf setting\n[client.rgw]\nrgw s3 auth require sigv4 = true\n```\n\n---\n\n### Finding 3 — 15-Minute Replay Attack Window with No Nonce Tracking\n\n**Severity:** Medium\n**File:** `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.h`, line 30\n**File:** `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc`, lines 265–278, 457–458\n\n#### Description\n\nThe request timestamp validation window (`RGW_AUTH_GRACE`) is set to **15 minutes** in both directions:\n\n```cpp\n// src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.h:30\nstatic constexpr auto RGW_AUTH_GRACE = std::chrono::minutes{15};\n\n// src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc:265-278\nbool is_time_skew_ok(time_t t)\n{\n  auto req_tp = ceph::coarse_real_clock::from_time_t(t);\n  auto cur_tp = ceph::coarse_real_clock::now();\n\n  if (std::chrono::abs(cur_tp - req_tp) > RGW_AUTH_GRACE) {\n    dout(10) << \"NOTICE: request time skew too big.\" << dendl;\n    return false;\n  }\n  return true;\n}\n```\n\nThis check is applied to V4 header-auth requests at `rgw_rest_s3.cc:457`. However, it is **not applied** to V2 presigned URLs (which use a fixed `Expires` epoch time) or V4 presigned URLs (which carry their own `X-Amz-Expires` duration, validated at `rgw_auth_s3.cc:308-318`).\n\nA 15-minute window means any captured signed request — for example, intercepted over an unencrypted connection or obtained from access logs — can be **replayed** by an attacker for up to 15 minutes. Since there is **no nonce or request ID tracking**, the gateway cannot distinguish a replayed request from a legitimate one.\n\n#### Remediation\n\n1. Make `RGW_AUTH_GRACE` configurable via a Ceph config option (e.g., `rgw_auth_grace_seconds`) so operators can reduce it to 5 minutes or less.\n2. Implement a short-lived replay cache: an LRU-bounded set of recently seen request signatures with TTL equal to the grace window. This prevents replay within the window at the cost of additional memory.\n3. Ensure that TLS is enforced for all RGW endpoints to reduce interception risk.\n\n---\n\n### Finding 4 — Unsigned Payload Accepted by Default\n\n**Severity:** Medium\n**File:** `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.h`, lines 637–659\n**File:** `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc`, lines 1199–1209\n\n#### Description\n\nWhen the `x-amz-content-sha256` header is absent from a request, the implementation silently defaults to `\"UNSIGNED-PAYLOAD\"`, meaning the HTTP request body is **not included in the signed material** and is not integrity-verified:\n\n```cpp\n// src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.h:637-659\nstatic inline const char* get_v4_exp_payload_hash(const req_info& info)\n{\n  const char *expected_request_payload_hash =\n    info.env->get(\"HTTP_X_AMZ_CONTENT_SHA256\");\n\n  if (!expected_request_payload_hash) {\n    // Falls back silently to UNSIGNED-PAYLOAD\n    expected_request_payload_hash = AWS4_UNSIGNED_PAYLOAD_HASH;\n  }\n  return expected_request_payload_hash;\n}\n```\n\nWhen `is_v4_payload_unsigned()` returns true, the payload completers (`AWSv4ComplSingle`, `AWSv4ComplMulti`) skip body-hash verification entirely. The streaming chunked case makes this explicit:\n\n```cpp\n// src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc:1207-1209\nif (flags & FLAG_UNSIGNED_CHUNKED) {\n  return false;   // signature check is completely skipped\n}\n```\n\nAn on-path attacker who intercepts a signed PUT/POST request (e.g., over HTTP without TLS) can **modify the request body** without invalidating the signature.\n\n#### Remediation\n\n1. Add a server-side configuration option to **reject `UNSIGNED-PAYLOAD` requests** for mutating operations (PUT, POST, DELETE) on sensitive buckets or globally.\n2. Log a warning when unsigned payload is accepted for write operations.\n3. Require clients to send `x-amz-content-sha256` with an actual hash for all mutating requests in high-security environments.\n\n---\n\n### Finding 5 — Signing-Key Chain and Signatures Written to Debug Logs\n\n**Severity:** Low\n**File:** `src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc`, lines 6321–6326\n**File:** `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc`, lines 996–999\n\n#### Description\n\nBoth the client-supplied signature and the server-computed signature are emitted to the Ceph debug log at verbosity level 15. The `string_to_sign` (which encodes the canonical request and timestamp) is logged at level 10. More critically, the **intermediate HMAC key derivation values** are also logged at level 10:\n\n```cpp\n// src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc:996-999\nldpp_dout(dpp, 10) << \"date_k    = \" << date_k << dendl;\nldpp_dout(dpp, 10) << \"region_k  = \" << region_k << dendl;\nldpp_dout(dpp, 10) << \"service_k = \" << service_k << dendl;\nldpp_dout(dpp, 10) << \"signing_k = \" << signing_key << dendl;\n```\n\nThe intermediate keys (`date_k`, `region_k`, `service_k`, `signing_key`) are derived deterministically from the user's secret key. An attacker with access to RGW debug logs at level 10 (a common diagnostic setting) can extract the `signing_key` and use it to **forge arbitrary requests** for the same user, date, region, and service without knowing the original secret key.\n\nThe signature values logged at level 15:\n```cpp\n// src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc:6321-6326\nldpp_dout(dpp, 15) << \"server signature=\" << server_signature << dendl;\nldpp_dout(dpp, 15) << \"client signature=\" << signature << dendl;\n```\n\n#### Remediation\n\n1. **Remove or redact** the `signing_key` and intermediate key log entries in `get_v4_signing_key()`. These have no legitimate diagnostic value that couldn't be served by a boolean \"signing key derived successfully\" message.\n2. Move signature value log entries to verbosity 20 or higher, or guard them behind a compile-time debug flag.\n3. Restrict filesystem permissions on RGW log files to mode 0600, owned by the RGW service account.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Summary Risk Assessment\n\n| # | Finding | Severity | Exploitability | Impact |\n|---|---------|----------|----------------|--------|\n| 1 | Non-constant-time signature comparison (timing oracle) | **High** | Moderate — requires many requests and network precision | Full auth bypass possible with sufficient measurements |\n| 2 | AWS Signature V2 (HMAC-SHA1) accepted without restriction | **High** | Low–Moderate — requires legacy/downgraded client | Weaker algorithm; body substitution on write ops |\n| 3 | 15-minute replay window, no nonce/request-ID tracking | **Medium** | Low — requires request interception | Captured signed requests replayable for 15 min |\n| 4 | Unsigned payload accepted by default for write operations | **Medium** | Moderate — requires MITM position | Body integrity not guaranteed on PUT/POST |\n| 5 | Signing-key chain and signatures in debug logs at level 10 | **Low** | Low — requires log file access | Signing key extractable; signature forgery possible |\n\n### Overall Risk Rating: **High**\n\nThe combination of a timing oracle in signature comparison (Finding 1) and continued unguarded support for the deprecated HMAC-SHA1-based V2 protocol (Finding 2) represents the most significant risk surface. Both are independently exploitable and together significantly weaken the authentication guarantees that S3 signature verification is intended to provide.\n\n### Recommended Priority Actions\n\n1. **Replace `signature.compare()` with constant-time comparison** (`src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc:6319`) — low-effort, high-impact fix.\n2. **Add `rgw_s3_auth_require_sigv4` config option** and enable it in security-hardened deployments — eliminates HMAC-SHA1 and body-substitution risk.\n3. **Make `RGW_AUTH_GRACE` configurable** and reduce it to 5 minutes for new deployments — reduces replay window.\n4. **Remove signing-key intermediate value logging** from `get_v4_signing_key()` (`src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc:996-999`) — prevents key material leakage via logs.\n\n---\n\n*Audit performed by static analysis of source code. No dynamic testing was conducted. Findings reflect code-level vulnerabilities; actual exploitability may vary depending on network topology, TLS deployment, and operator configuration.*\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":3,"cache_creation_input_tokens":374,"cache_read_input_tokens":60524,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":374,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"c88aed4d-2e4d-45dd-9dd5-999fcfab4d26","uuid":"44acd2b4-65b3-4cfa-b347-702b9940761f"}
{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01BTHQEdbPrNenANN1m3oefP","type":"tool_result","content":"File created successfully at: /workspace/security_audit.md"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"c88aed4d-2e4d-45dd-9dd5-999fcfab4d26","uuid":"cebb56b2-0e9f-4561-9790-1020a6d2015b","tool_use_result":{"type":"create","filePath":"/workspace/security_audit.md","content":"# Security Audit: Ceph RADOS Gateway S3 Authentication\n\n**Date:** 2026-03-08\n**Scope:** AWS Signature V2/V4 authentication implementation in `src/rgw/`\n**Repository:** `github.com/sg-evals/ceph--v19.2.1`\n\n---\n\n## 1. Authentication Flow Overview\n\nThe S3 authentication flow in Ceph RGW is implemented across the following files:\n\n| File | Role |\n|------|------|\n| `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.h` | Auth strategy classes, V4 constants, time-skew check declaration |\n| `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc` | Canonical header/query construction, signing-key derivation, V2/V4 HMAC computation |\n| `src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.h` | `AWSEngine`, `VersionAbstractor`, V2/V4 abstractor class declarations |\n| `src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc` | Auth data extraction, version detection, `LocalEngine::authenticate()` |\n| `src/rgw/rgw_auth.h` | Core `Identity` and `Engine` interfaces |\n\n### Key Functions\n\n```\nAWSGeneralAbstractor::get_auth_data()     rgw_rest_s3.cc:5556\n  └─ discover_aws_flavour()               → determines V2 or V4\n  └─ get_auth_data_v2()                   rgw_rest_s3.cc:5988  (HMAC-SHA1)\n  └─ get_auth_data_v4()                   rgw_rest_s3.cc:5570  (HMAC-SHA256)\n\nLocalEngine::authenticate()               rgw_rest_s3.cc:6265\n  └─ signature_factory(cct, k.key, ...)   → compute server-side signature\n  └─ signature.compare(server_signature)  → compare (line 6319)\n\nget_v4_signature()                        rgw_auth_s3.cc:1013\n  └─ get_v4_signing_key()                 → HMAC-SHA256 key derivation chain\n  └─ calc_hmac_sha256(signing_key, ...)   → final digest\n\nget_v2_signature()                        rgw_auth_s3.cc:1037\n  └─ calc_hmac_sha1(secret_key, ...)      → HMAC-SHA1 digest + base64\n\nis_time_skew_ok()                         rgw_auth_s3.cc:265\n  └─ RGW_AUTH_GRACE = 15 minutes          rgw_auth_s3.h:30\n```\n\n---\n\n## 2. Security Findings\n\n---\n\n### Finding 1 — Non-Constant-Time Signature Comparison (Timing Attack)\n\n**Severity:** High\n**File:** `src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc`, line 6319\n**File:** `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc`, lines 1228, 1231\n\n#### Description\n\nThe final signature comparison in `LocalEngine::authenticate()` uses `std::string::compare()`, which is **not constant-time**. An attacker can exploit measurable timing differences to learn, one byte at a time, whether a forged signature prefix matches the expected server signature. This enables a remote timing oracle attack against HMAC-SHA256 (V4) and HMAC-SHA1 (V2) signatures.\n\n#### Code Reference\n\n```cpp\n// src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc:6317-6330\nconst VersionAbstractor::server_signature_t server_signature = \\\n  signature_factory(cct, k.key, string_to_sign);\nauto compare = signature.compare(server_signature);   // <-- NOT constant-time\n\nldpp_dout(dpp, 15) << \"server signature=\" << server_signature << dendl;\nldpp_dout(dpp, 15) << \"client signature=\" << signature << dendl;\n\nif (compare != 0) {\n  return result_t::reject(-ERR_SIGNATURE_NO_MATCH);\n}\n```\n\nThe same issue appears in chunk signature verification:\n\n```cpp\n// src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc:1225-1232\nauto match_signatures = [&]() -> bool {\n  if (chunk_meta.get_offset() == 0) [[unlikely]] {\n    return chunk_meta.get_signature() == prev_chunk_signature;  // <-- NOT constant-time\n  }\n  return chunk_meta.get_signature() == calc_signature;          // <-- NOT constant-time\n};\n```\n\n`std::string::operator==` and `std::string::compare()` are permitted by the C++ standard to short-circuit on the first mismatched byte, exposing timing differences measurable over a network in controlled conditions.\n\n#### Remediation\n\nReplace all signature comparisons with a constant-time comparison function such as `CRYPTO_memcmp()` (OpenSSL), `timingsafe_bcmp()` (BSD), or a dedicated implementation:\n\n```cpp\n// Constant-time comparison\nbool signatures_equal = (server_signature.size() == signature.size()) &&\n    (CRYPTO_memcmp(server_signature.data(),\n                   signature.data(),\n                   server_signature.size()) == 0);\nif (!signatures_equal) {\n  return result_t::reject(-ERR_SIGNATURE_NO_MATCH);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### Finding 2 — AWS Signature Version 2 (HMAC-SHA1) Supported Without Restriction\n\n**Severity:** High\n**File:** `src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc`, lines 5556–5574, 5988–6068\n**File:** `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc`, lines 1037–1062\n\n#### Description\n\nThe gateway transparently supports AWS Signature Version 2, which uses **HMAC-SHA1** with a significantly weaker security posture than V4:\n\n- SHA-1 is considered **cryptographically weakened** for collision resistance (HMAC-SHA1 offers only 80-bit security vs. 128-bit for HMAC-SHA256).\n- V2 does **not** include the HTTP body or most headers in the signed material, making it vulnerable to request body substitution attacks.\n- V2 presigned URLs use an epoch-based `Expires` value and are not protected against relay attacks across regions.\n- AWS itself deprecated Signature V2 and began blocking it in regions after 2020.\n\nThe version selection is fully transparent to the server — whichever version the client presents is accepted, with no operator-visible warning:\n\n```cpp\n// src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc:5555-5574\nAWSGeneralAbstractor::get_auth_data(const req_state* const s) const\n{\n  AwsVersion version;\n  AwsRoute route;\n  std::tie(version, route) = discover_aws_flavour(s->info);\n  // ...\n  if (version == AwsVersion::V2) {\n    return get_auth_data_v2(s);           // uses HMAC-SHA1, no warning logged\n  } else if (version == AwsVersion::V4) {\n    return get_auth_data_v4(s, ...);      // uses HMAC-SHA256\n  }\n}\n\n// src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc:1037-1062\nget_v2_signature(CephContext* const cct,\n                 const std::string& secret_key,\n                 const AWSEngine::VersionAbstractor::string_to_sign_t& string_to_sign)\n{\n  // ...\n  const auto digest = calc_hmac_sha1(secret_key, string_to_sign);  // HMAC-SHA1\n  // ...\n}\n```\n\n#### Remediation\n\n1. Add a Ceph configuration option (e.g., `rgw_s3_auth_require_sigv4`) to **deny V2 requests** in production deployments.\n2. Log a warning at operator-visible log level (0 or 1) whenever a V2 request is accepted.\n3. Audit presigned-URL handling separately — V2 presigned URLs allow body substitution because `Content-MD5` inclusion is optional in V2's canonical string.\n\n```ini\n# Recommended ceph.conf setting\n[client.rgw]\nrgw s3 auth require sigv4 = true\n```\n\n---\n\n### Finding 3 — 15-Minute Replay Attack Window with No Nonce Tracking\n\n**Severity:** Medium\n**File:** `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.h`, line 30\n**File:** `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc`, lines 265–278, 457–458\n\n#### Description\n\nThe request timestamp validation window (`RGW_AUTH_GRACE`) is set to **15 minutes** in both directions:\n\n```cpp\n// src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.h:30\nstatic constexpr auto RGW_AUTH_GRACE = std::chrono::minutes{15};\n\n// src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc:265-278\nbool is_time_skew_ok(time_t t)\n{\n  auto req_tp = ceph::coarse_real_clock::from_time_t(t);\n  auto cur_tp = ceph::coarse_real_clock::now();\n\n  if (std::chrono::abs(cur_tp - req_tp) > RGW_AUTH_GRACE) {\n    dout(10) << \"NOTICE: request time skew too big.\" << dendl;\n    return false;\n  }\n  return true;\n}\n```\n\nThis check is applied to V4 header-auth requests at `rgw_rest_s3.cc:457`. However, it is **not applied** to V2 presigned URLs (which use a fixed `Expires` epoch time) or V4 presigned URLs (which carry their own `X-Amz-Expires` duration, validated at `rgw_auth_s3.cc:308-318`).\n\nA 15-minute window means any captured signed request — for example, intercepted over an unencrypted connection or obtained from access logs — can be **replayed** by an attacker for up to 15 minutes. Since there is **no nonce or request ID tracking**, the gateway cannot distinguish a replayed request from a legitimate one.\n\n#### Remediation\n\n1. Make `RGW_AUTH_GRACE` configurable via a Ceph config option (e.g., `rgw_auth_grace_seconds`) so operators can reduce it to 5 minutes or less.\n2. Implement a short-lived replay cache: an LRU-bounded set of recently seen request signatures with TTL equal to the grace window. This prevents replay within the window at the cost of additional memory.\n3. Ensure that TLS is enforced for all RGW endpoints to reduce interception risk.\n\n---\n\n### Finding 4 — Unsigned Payload Accepted by Default\n\n**Severity:** Medium\n**File:** `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.h`, lines 637–659\n**File:** `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc`, lines 1199–1209\n\n#### Description\n\nWhen the `x-amz-content-sha256` header is absent from a request, the implementation silently defaults to `\"UNSIGNED-PAYLOAD\"`, meaning the HTTP request body is **not included in the signed material** and is not integrity-verified:\n\n```cpp\n// src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.h:637-659\nstatic inline const char* get_v4_exp_payload_hash(const req_info& info)\n{\n  const char *expected_request_payload_hash =\n    info.env->get(\"HTTP_X_AMZ_CONTENT_SHA256\");\n\n  if (!expected_request_payload_hash) {\n    // Falls back silently to UNSIGNED-PAYLOAD\n    expected_request_payload_hash = AWS4_UNSIGNED_PAYLOAD_HASH;\n  }\n  return expected_request_payload_hash;\n}\n```\n\nWhen `is_v4_payload_unsigned()` returns true, the payload completers (`AWSv4ComplSingle`, `AWSv4ComplMulti`) skip body-hash verification entirely. The streaming chunked case makes this explicit:\n\n```cpp\n// src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc:1207-1209\nif (flags & FLAG_UNSIGNED_CHUNKED) {\n  return false;   // signature check is completely skipped\n}\n```\n\nAn on-path attacker who intercepts a signed PUT/POST request (e.g., over HTTP without TLS) can **modify the request body** without invalidating the signature.\n\n#### Remediation\n\n1. Add a server-side configuration option to **reject `UNSIGNED-PAYLOAD` requests** for mutating operations (PUT, POST, DELETE) on sensitive buckets or globally.\n2. Log a warning when unsigned payload is accepted for write operations.\n3. Require clients to send `x-amz-content-sha256` with an actual hash for all mutating requests in high-security environments.\n\n---\n\n### Finding 5 — Signing-Key Chain and Signatures Written to Debug Logs\n\n**Severity:** Low\n**File:** `src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc`, lines 6321–6326\n**File:** `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc`, lines 996–999\n\n#### Description\n\nBoth the client-supplied signature and the server-computed signature are emitted to the Ceph debug log at verbosity level 15. The `string_to_sign` (which encodes the canonical request and timestamp) is logged at level 10. More critically, the **intermediate HMAC key derivation values** are also logged at level 10:\n\n```cpp\n// src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc:996-999\nldpp_dout(dpp, 10) << \"date_k    = \" << date_k << dendl;\nldpp_dout(dpp, 10) << \"region_k  = \" << region_k << dendl;\nldpp_dout(dpp, 10) << \"service_k = \" << service_k << dendl;\nldpp_dout(dpp, 10) << \"signing_k = \" << signing_key << dendl;\n```\n\nThe intermediate keys (`date_k`, `region_k`, `service_k`, `signing_key`) are derived deterministically from the user's secret key. An attacker with access to RGW debug logs at level 10 (a common diagnostic setting) can extract the `signing_key` and use it to **forge arbitrary requests** for the same user, date, region, and service without knowing the original secret key.\n\nThe signature values logged at level 15:\n```cpp\n// src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc:6321-6326\nldpp_dout(dpp, 15) << \"server signature=\" << server_signature << dendl;\nldpp_dout(dpp, 15) << \"client signature=\" << signature << dendl;\n```\n\n#### Remediation\n\n1. **Remove or redact** the `signing_key` and intermediate key log entries in `get_v4_signing_key()`. These have no legitimate diagnostic value that couldn't be served by a boolean \"signing key derived successfully\" message.\n2. Move signature value log entries to verbosity 20 or higher, or guard them behind a compile-time debug flag.\n3. Restrict filesystem permissions on RGW log files to mode 0600, owned by the RGW service account.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Summary Risk Assessment\n\n| # | Finding | Severity | Exploitability | Impact |\n|---|---------|----------|----------------|--------|\n| 1 | Non-constant-time signature comparison (timing oracle) | **High** | Moderate — requires many requests and network precision | Full auth bypass possible with sufficient measurements |\n| 2 | AWS Signature V2 (HMAC-SHA1) accepted without restriction | **High** | Low–Moderate — requires legacy/downgraded client | Weaker algorithm; body substitution on write ops |\n| 3 | 15-minute replay window, no nonce/request-ID tracking | **Medium** | Low — requires request interception | Captured signed requests replayable for 15 min |\n| 4 | Unsigned payload accepted by default for write operations | **Medium** | Moderate — requires MITM position | Body integrity not guaranteed on PUT/POST |\n| 5 | Signing-key chain and signatures in debug logs at level 10 | **Low** | Low — requires log file access | Signing key extractable; signature forgery possible |\n\n### Overall Risk Rating: **High**\n\nThe combination of a timing oracle in signature comparison (Finding 1) and continued unguarded support for the deprecated HMAC-SHA1-based V2 protocol (Finding 2) represents the most significant risk surface. Both are independently exploitable and together significantly weaken the authentication guarantees that S3 signature verification is intended to provide.\n\n### Recommended Priority Actions\n\n1. **Replace `signature.compare()` with constant-time comparison** (`src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc:6319`) — low-effort, high-impact fix.\n2. **Add `rgw_s3_auth_require_sigv4` config option** and enable it in security-hardened deployments — eliminates HMAC-SHA1 and body-substitution risk.\n3. **Make `RGW_AUTH_GRACE` configurable** and reduce it to 5 minutes for new deployments — reduces replay window.\n4. **Remove signing-key intermediate value logging** from `get_v4_signing_key()` (`src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc:996-999`) — prevents key material leakage via logs.\n\n---\n\n*Audit performed by static analysis of source code. No dynamic testing was conducted. Findings reflect code-level vulnerabilities; actual exploitability may vary depending on network topology, TLS deployment, and operator configuration.*\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
